My face always felt rough, even though I have tried to exfoliate with other facial scrubs--it has a very unhealthy texture and I was breaking out way more than a 30 year old should. After just one use of Cure, I immediately felt a difference in texture and appearance. The &amp;#34;white balls&amp;#34; that form are definitely dead skin because the gel is not goopy (it&#x27;s rather liquidy) and it does not congeal. It&#x27;s pricier, but the instructions recommend 3-5 pumps, twice a week, which is really not that much considering how small the pump is so one bottle should last a while. Definitely adding this to my normal skincare routine!</li>

    <li> This exfoliator really does live up to the hype. I count on it to rid my skin of dead cells before cleaning at least 2-3 times a week. However, I have relatively hardy skin, and I disagree with the claim that it can be used daily. It is far too wasteful to use it that way. It also is possible to over exfoliate with this product, though it doesn&#x27;t hurt or sting like a physical or stronger chemical exfoliator will. I noticed my skin getting a bit irritated (bumpy) and oily if I overused this (around my nose and mouth, for the most part), so I recommend using it every other day at most. It can also be a bit drying if you don&#x27;t continue with the rest of your skincare routine soon after you use it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall: Fantastic product, but use judgement and treat it as you would any other exfoliant.</li>

    <li> So I was sold on all the positive reviews, before buying... and that&#x27;s why I bought this.  In the back of my mind, I didn&#x27;t know what to expect.    Some background: I&#x27;m a 37-year old fair-skinned Asian-American male.  I have had a facial skincare routine every day of my life since I turned 30 years old.  For 5 years, as far as cleansing goes, I was always using Stridex daily, and 2x a month using an acid exfoliator (the Olay serum/scrub kit).  For the last couple years, I have switched to a basic water-based cleanser, and every 6-12 weeks I have applied either a 15% or 25% TCA chemical peel. In other words, I&#x27;m no stranger to what exfoliation feels like.    As a kid, growing up, in the bath or shower, I would often scratch or rub my arms or legs to really give myself a deep clean.  It would produce these \\&quot;strands\\&quot; of dead epidermis.  But I would have to rub those areas really hard.    Well, this \\&quot;CURE\\&quot; gel basically eliminates the need for all that rubbing/scratching.  You rub gently over your face and within 15 seconds, sure enough, the epidermis starts to flake or \\&quot;ball\\&quot; off!    Now, before I purchased, I read some people saying that if this was really your skin, that you&#x27;d be suffering from burns on your face.  And I have two responses: (1) each time I apply this \\&quot;CURE\\&quot; gel, I squirt 4 pumps into my hands, and cover my face with it, and it appears to take off somewhere between 1/3 to 1/2 of (the dead stratum corneum layer of) my epidermis skin layer; and (2) a lot of the skin that is flaking or balling off is actually from your HANDS, not your face!    Of course, you&#x27;ve read the reviews that claim that this product does nothing.    Well, so I ran all the following tests:    (a) First, when I wore a plastic glove and rubbed the gel between my fingers, there was absolutely ZERO balling, even after rubbing 3 minutes until it dried.  So, that basically eliminated all these claims in these negative 1-star reviews that it was due to coagulation of the gel.    (b) Then,I applied the lotion once, rinsed off, applied again, rinsed off, and applied again, rinsed off.  Each of those 3 times I had the balling/flaking results.  3 times!  Now, a note: by the time I rinsed off the third time, my skin was dry and stinging.  It was the same kind of stinging I get from applying a 15% TCA peel!  Maybe not as strong, so maybe it&#x27;s similar to a 7% TCA peel, but the sensation is definitely the same.  And that stinging sensation comes where the TCA peel most affects me--around my nostrils, and under my chin.    (c) My third experiment was on a separate evening, where I applied the lotion with a plastic glove (you can also wear a plastic sandwich bag, like a glove, instead).  This time, on the 3rd pass, I no longer got the balling/flaking results.  Instead, when I used the leftover gel from this 3rd pass attempt on my forearm, well, the dead epidermis started to ball/flake.    (d) My last experiment was to try applying this in the shower.  And it didn&#x27;t work!  This gel doesn&#x27;t work at all if you try to apply it to a wet face.  It only works (and works REALLY well!) if you apply it to a clean dry face!!!    The results are remarkable.  My skin is glowing after using this product.    So after reading all this, what am I trying to tell you?:    #1:  This stuff is for real, most definitely.  The stuff balling up is most definitely your dead epidermis.    #2:  It&#x27;s best to apply this with something, instead of direct contact with your hands.  I will continue using a plastic glove or plastic bag to apply.    #3.  If you decide to apply this 2-3 times in a row, you may exfoliate all your epidermis, and you better cover up with an SPF lotion.    #4.  Only apply on a dry face!    I hope this helps some of you in your usage or purchasing decisions.  Cheers.    1-WEEK UPDATE: If you wear a plastic glove while applying, you may need to rub with significantly more pressure because the plastic is slick and there&#x27;s no friction to rub the surface epidermis away.But more amazingly, after about a week of use, it has gently removed about 30% of a discoloration caused by a popped pimple.  Usually I have to wait months for it to go away, or I use deep exfoliation on it and it gets irritated and sticks around longer. Finally, after a week of use, I&#x27;ve also discovered that my Ponds pore strips are much more effective now on my pores.  Overall, I&#x27;m convinced that the balling of skin looks so strange because it is an agglomeration (&#x27;mixture&#x27;) of both your dead skin and the product itself (which isn&#x27;t so far-fetched given that the product isn&#x27;t supposed to necessarily magically disappear!). I&#x27;m quite happy with the gentleness of this product.</li>

    <li> As the gel dries it rolls up into little bits/balls which look like dead skin cells, making you THINK it&#x27;s your skin being gently exfoliated. However the bits are NOT your dead skin cells, they are formed by the product. You can easily do a little experiment: Put on rubber or latex free gloves, place a small amount of product on one gloved hand and rub with the other glove hand, you&#x27;ll see the same bits form, no skin involved.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;~*Ingredients*~&lt;br /&gt;-Water&lt;br /&gt;-Glycerin&lt;br /&gt;-C10-30, alkyl acrylate crosspolymer: Thickeners that when rubbed form little bits/balls with this particular formula.&lt;br /&gt;~*With Microscopic Amounts of the following*~&lt;br /&gt;-Dicocodimonium:  Emulsifier&lt;br /&gt;-Chloride: Type of chloride is NOT revealed :-(&lt;br /&gt;-Steartrimonium Bromide: Can&#x27;t imagine why this would be in any product for face/skin. It&#x27;s usually found in hair products. Considered a moderate hazard ingredient by the Cosmetics Database. The EWG lists warning regarding concentration limits, allergic reactions, and organ system toxicity due to animal studies that showed brain and nervous system effects and skin irritation at moderate doses and broad systematic effects at low doses. It is also considered a human toxicant by the CIR. Is &#x27;considered&#x27; safe for use in hair rinse-off products and for use at concentrations of up to 0.25% in leave-on hair products. Dermal exposure is &#x27;considered&#x27; safe up to 2%.&lt;br /&gt;-Aloe: We all know this one :-)&lt;br /&gt;-Gingko Biloba Extract:  Antibacterial and Anti-fungal properties&lt;br /&gt;-Rosmarinus officinalis/Rosemary leaf extract: Antimicrobial Agent; Antioxidant; Fragrance Ingredient; Skin-Conditioning Agent; Occlusive; perfuming&lt;br /&gt;-Butylene Glycol: Chemical Preservative&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;**TRUE EXFOLIATION can be achieved either mechanically by scrubbing/massaging the skin with a liquid containing small, hard particles (scrubs), also chemically by applying products containing active ingredients with a peeling effect (e.g. alpha-hydroxy acids, beta-hydroxy acids and others).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt; *** MAKE YOUR OWN EXFOLIANT: Mix a little olive oil and sugar and use to exfoliate face and body. I wanted a gentle exfoliator since I have sensitive skin, and I felt like gritty exfoliators never did the trick or were too harsh. I got the Skin79 Crystal peeling Gel and it worked well! I had that one for over a year and I was running low so I decided to finally get Cure as the price per mL was cheaper than the Skin79 one. I&#x27;ll sort of compare the two, so maybe that will help you decide on something.&lt;br /&gt;The first thing I noticed about Cure was that the gel is quite watery. Use small pumps when applying it to your face so that it doesn&#x27;t drip through your fingers. There is a very faint scent of alcohol but it isn&#x27;t noticeable or irritating. Skin79&#x27;s gel is more gel-like and thicker, which I think is easier in the application. There is, however, a very heavy scent, and although it is pleasant, I&#x27;d prefer no scent as fragrances can irritate the skin. When applying either, it&#x27;s best to apply a good layer that covers your skin. If it&#x27;s too thin, it will dry before you can really rub a lot of the skin off, and if it&#x27;s too thick, it&#x27;ll waste product and be quite messy. I find that applying a layer all over your face and waiting about 45 seconds before rubbing makes it easer than just rubbing the hell out of your skin. The product needs a bit of time to start working, and you can see parts of dead skin turning whitish when you let the product sit on it. If you start rubbing right after you apply it, you&#x27;ll be rubbing for a while before you get any clumps. Both products make your skin clump similarly, but I think Cure dries a bit faster because it&#x27;s more liquid-y, so it might be easier to work in sections (like do the bottom half of your face and then your forehead). Both leave great results; visibly smoother and softer skin. Exfoliating helps minimize acne, as there is less dead skin clogging up your pores. Use it weekly for the best results (don&#x27;t use it every day as that might inflame your skin and waste product ). And for those that think it&#x27;s fake or that it&#x27;s the product and not your skin that is clumping up, it&#x27;s not. I&#x27;ve tested both on my bathroom tiles and nothing ever clumps up. I&#x27;ve also tried exfoliating back to back and while the first time there was a lot of dead skin, the second time there was barely any (because you exfoliated most of the dead skin off). I definitely recommend this to people with sensitive and acne-prone skin! You might want to try the Skin79 one before shelling out the money for this, but this big bottle of Cure will last quite a while!</li>

    <li> Cure Natural . Exfoliators, as you probably know, work typically work in one of two ways: by chemically loosening dead skin cells with an alpha hydroxy acid or similar chemical. Or by mechanically removing dead skin cells with an abrasive particle like a walnut shell or a polyethylene bead. This product contains neither type of ingredient. It does, however, contain Activated Hydrogen Water? The balls are formed as the water evaporates and the acrylates polymer comes out of solution. (Some products like this claim that the balls are actually the dead skin cells but thats not true.) I suppose the balls could give some degree of exfoliation but I wonder if theyd work as well as particles specifically sized for that task. the plastic micro-bead issue plays out. They gained popularity because they are less abrasive than walnut shells and other similar exfoliators. Now theyre losing popularity become of their environmental impact. thebeautybrains.com</li>
